   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Voiced palatal fricative
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">

      <p>
       The
       <b>
        voiced palatal fricative
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound, used in some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_communication" title="Speech communication">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       (IPA) that represents this sound is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʝ
       </span>
       ⟩ (crossed-tail j), and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        j\
       </code>
       . It is the non-sibilant equivalent of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_sibilant" title="Voiced palatal sibilant">
        voiced palatal sibilant
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broad_transcription" title="Broad transcription">
        broad transcription
       </a>
       , the symbol for the
       <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant" title="Palatal approximant">
        palatal approximant
       </a>
       , ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        j
       </span>
       ⟩, may be used for the sake of simplicity.
      </p>
      <p>
       The voiced palatal fricative is a very rare sound, occurring in only seven of the 317 languages surveyed by the original
       <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Phonological_Segment_Inventory_Database" title="UCLA Phonological Segment Inventory Database">
        UCLA Phonological Segment Inventory Database
       </a>
       . In
       <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">
        Kabyle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Margi_language" title="Margi language">
        Margi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek" title="Modern Greek">
        Modern Greek
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">
        Scottish Gaelic
       </a>
       , the sound occurs phonemically, along with its
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">
        voiceless counterpart
       </a>
       , and in several more, the sound occurs a result of phonological processes.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also the
       <b>
        voiced post-palatal fricative
       </b>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in some languages, which is articulated slightly more back compared with the place of articulation of the prototypical voiced palatal fricative but not as back as the prototypical
       <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">
        voiced velar fricative
       </a>
       . The International Phonetic Alphabet does not have a separate symbol for that sound, but it can be transcribed as ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʝ̠
       </span>
       ⟩, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʝ˗
       </span>
       ⟩ (both symbols denote a
       <a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Advanced_and_retracted" title="Relative articulation">
        retracted
       </a>
       ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ʝ
       </span>
       ⟩), ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɣ̟
       </span>
       ⟩ or ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɣ˖
       </span>
       ⟩ (both symbols denote an
       <a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Advanced_and_retracted" title="Relative articulation">
        advanced
       </a>
       ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɣ
       </span>
       ⟩). The equivalent X-SAMPA symbols are
       <code>
        j\_-
       </code>
       and
       <code>
        G_+
       </code>
       , respectively.
      </p>
      <p>
       Especially in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broad_transcription" title="Broad transcription">
        broad transcription
       </a>
       , the voiced post-palatal fricative may be transcribed as a palatalized voiced velar fricative (⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɣʲ
       </span>
       ⟩ in the IPA,
       <code>
        G'
       </code>
       or
       <code>
        G_j
       </code>
       in X-SAMPA).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Voiced_palatal_fricative&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced palatal fricative:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
         fricative
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by constricting air flow through a narrow channel at the place of articulation, causing
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulence
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Palatal_consonant" title="Palatal consonant">
         palatal
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the middle or back part of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        raised to the
        <a href="/wiki/Hard_palate" title="Hard palate">
         hard palate
        </a>
        . The otherwise identical post-palatal variant is articulated slightly behind the hard palate, making it sound slightly closer to the velar
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">
          ɣ
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream along the center of the tongue, rather than to the sides.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>

                       </div>
                       <p>
                        Where symbols appear in pairs, the leftmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">
                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
                       </p>

                        Shaded areas denote articulations judged to be impossible.
